(i) Generating pool-based assemblies: the Roche/454 Titanium reads were independently assembled for each pool to obtain pool-wise assembled contigs. PE reads corresponding to each chromosome were mapped to the contigs of the respective chromosomes and PE reads belonging to each chromosome pool were extracted. A second round of assembly with both Titanium and PE reads corresponding to each pool was performed to obtain pool-level scaffolds. (ii) Incorporation of WGS reads into pool-wise assemblies: to identify WGS reads corresponding to each chromosome pool, the WGS reads were separately assembled in combination with PE reads from all 12 chromosomes, and the WGS scaffolds corresponding to each pool were identified by comparing the scaffolds to the pool-wise scaffolds obtained in the previous step using BLASTN<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Altschul, S.F., Gish, W., Miller, W., Myers, E.W. &amp; Lipman, D.J. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. 215, 403–410 (1990)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d86e2943">52</a></sup>. WGS reads corresponding to each pool were then extracted, and a third round of assembly was performed with the Titanium, PE and WGS reads for each pool. (iii) Identification of misassembled scaffolds: each scaffold was aligned to the corresponding chromosome of the <i>O. sativa</i> ssp. <i>japonica</i> reference sequence (RefSeq)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="International Rice Genome Sequencing Project. The map-based sequence of the rice genome. Nature 436, 793–800 (2005)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d86e2954">11</a></sup> using Nucmer<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Kurtz, S. et al. Versatile and open software for comparing large genomes. Genome Biol. 5, R12 (2004)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d86e2958">53</a></sup>, and potential misassembled scaffolds and misassembly breakpoints were identified. Putative misassemblies in scaffolds were evaluated by inspecting PE depth and Titanium depth across each breakpoint. Any scaffolds that had a PE depth ≤1 and coverage of ≤4× were confirmed as misassemblies, and each scaffold was split at the breakpoints into multiple scaffolds. (iv) Merging of overlapping regions between pools: to remove any redundant sequences between adjacent pools, scaffolds from neighboring pools were aligned using Nucmer, and redundant regions were identified. Reads from overlapping scaffolds were extracted and reassembled to generate a non-redundant set of scaffolds. This process was repeated for all neighboring pools for all chromosomes to obtain a non-redundant set of scaffolds for each chromosome. (v) Ordering and orienting of scaffolds: scaffolds for each chromosome were aligned with the corresponding chromosome of the <i>O. sativa</i> ssp. <i>japonica</i> reference genome using Nucmer, and the scaffolds were grouped into either the mapped or unmapped category. All mapped scaffolds were ordered and oriented as per the <i>O. sativa</i> ssp. <i>japonica</i> chromosomes. (vi) Incorporation of Sanger sequences: as a final step, the existing Sanger BAC sequences from the short arm of chromosome 3 and from chromosomes 6, 8, 11 and 12 were spliced into the existing 454 assembly. The 454 scaffolds corresponding to Sanger sequences were identified by BLASTN, and the 454 scaffolds were replaced by the Sanger sequences.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">Protein-coding and tRNA gene predictions.</h3><p>Gene models were determined using a combination approach of a consensus prediction from <i>ab initio</i> gene predictions (Fgenesh++<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Salamov, A.A. &amp; Solovyev, V.V. Ab initio gene finding in Drosophila genomic DNA. Genome Res. 10, 516–522 (2000)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d86e2985">54</a></sup>, ProtoMap<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Yona, G., Linial, N. &amp; Linial, M. ProtoMap: automatic classification of protein sequences and hierarchy of protein families. Nucleic Acids Res. 28, 49–55 (2000)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d86e2989">55</a></sup> and GeneID<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Parra, G., Blanco, E. &amp; Guigo, R. GeneID in Drosophila. Genome Res. 10, 511–515 (2000)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d86e2993">13</a></sup>) and an optimal spliced alignment from protein and transcript homology searches using GenomeThreader<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Gremme, G., Brendel, V., Sparks, M.E. &amp; Kurtz, S. Engineering a software tool for gene structure prediction in higher organisms. Inf. Softw. Technol. 47, 965–978 (2005)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d86e2997">56</a></sup> with a splice site model for rice. Homologous protein evidence mappings were derived from annotations of the following finished plant genome projects: <i>O. sativa</i> (version TIGR6.1 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Ouyang, S. et al. The TIGR Rice Genome Annotation Resource: improvements and new features. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, D883–D887 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d86e3004">57</a>) and RAP2 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Rice Annotation Project. The Rice Annotation Project Database (RAP-DB): 2008 update. Nucleic Acids Res. 36, D1028–D1033 (2008)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d86e3007">58</a>)), <i>Sorghum bicolor</i> (high confidence set of version 1.4)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Paterson, A.H. et al. The Sorghum bicolor genome and the diversification of grasses. Nature 457, 551–556 (2009)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d86e3014">59</a></sup>, <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i> (version TAIR9)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Lamesch, P. et al. The Arabidopsis Information Resource (TAIR): improved gene annotation and new tools. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, D1202–D1210 (2012)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d86e3022">60</a></sup> and <i>Brachypodium</i> (version 1.2)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="International Brachypodium Initiative. Genome sequencing and analysis of the model grass Brachypodium distachyon. Nature 463, 763–768 (2010)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d86e3029">61</a></sup>. Optimal spliced alignments of TIGR transcript assemblies<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Childs, K.L. et al. The TIGR Plant Transcript Assemblies database. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, D846–D851 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d86e3033">62</a></sup>, comprising several monocotyledonous species (<i>Zea mays</i>, <i>Saccharum officinale</i>, <i>O. sativa</i>, <i>Hordeum vulgare</i>, <i>Triticum aestivum</i> and <i>Brachypodium distachyon</i>) as well as assembled RNA-Seq reads of <i>O. glaberrima</i>, were used for gene predictions based on homology and/or experimental evidence. Additionally, Markov models and position-specific scoring matrices were applied to estimate the coding potential for the models without protein homology and to evaluate splice site and start and stop codons, respectively. We used coding sequences for the Markov models that had a minimum protein similarity and alignment coverage of ≥95% to known <i>O. sativa</i> models, a minimum mean expression of three RNA-Seq reads and coverage ≥98% by RNA-Seq reads. The gene models without homology, i.e., <i>E</i> value greater than 10<sup>−10</sup>, were selected for a minimum size of at least 60 amino acids, minimum coding potential &gt;0, maximal overlap with repeats of 20% and mean RNA-Seq expression &gt;0.5. tRNA genes were identified with tRNAscan-SE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Lowe, T.M. tRNAscan-SE: a program for improved detection of transfer RNA genes in genomic sequence. Nucleic Acids Res. 25, 955–964 (1997)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d86e3068">14</a></sup> using default parameters.</p><p>The flowering time, light response and WRKY genes were selected from the <i>O. sativa</i> ssp. <i>japonica</i> RefSeq. The orthologous genes in <i>O. glaberrima</i> were determined using MegaBLAST with an identity of 90% for flowering time and light response genes. The orthologous WRKY genes in <i>O. glaberrima</i> and <i>O. brachyantha</i> were determined by tBLASTN using the conserved domain and predicted proteins from the <i>O. sativa</i> ssp. <i>japonica</i> genome annotation. Translated proteins with identity and coverage greater than 80% were considered in the analysis. We further checked the syntenic region to confirm the orthologous status of these genes.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">RNA sequencing and analysis.</h3><p>The <i>O. glaberrima</i>, <i>O. barthii</i>, <i>O. sativa</i> ssp. <i>japonica</i>, <i>O. rufipogon</i> and <i>O. nivara</i> accessions used for RNA-Seq analysis were obtained from the International Rice Research Institute (IRRI) Genetic Resource Center (GRC). Leaf tissue for library construction was collected from plants at the four-leaf stage. Root tissue for library construction was collected from plants growing in hydroponic conditions. The panicles were collected at different stages of flower development for the construction of sequencing libraries. Strand-specific RNA-Seq libraries of the different species were constructed using the protocol described previously<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Wang, L. et al. A low-cost library construction protocol and data analysis pipeline for Illumina-based strand-specific multiplex RNA-seq. PLoS ONE 6, e26426 (2011)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d86e3124">63</a></sup> and sequenced on one lane of an Illumina HiSeq 2000 instrument. Raw pair-end reads were <i>de novo</i> assembled using Trinity r2012-05-18 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Grabherr, M.G. et al. Full-length transcriptome assembly from RNA-Seq data without a reference genome. Nat. Biotechnol. 29, 644–652 (2011)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d86e3130">64</a>). The assembled sequences were aligned to <i>O. sativa</i> ssp. <i>japonica</i> RefSeq using Bowtie V2.1.0 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Langmead, B., Trapnell, C., Pop, M. &amp; Salzberg, S.L. Ultrafast and memory-efficient alignment of short DNA sequences to the human genome. Genome Biol. 10, R25 (2009)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d86e3140">65</a>). The results of the alignment were visualized and annotated using the Integrative Genomics Viewer (IGV) V2.3 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Robinson, J.T. et al. Integrative genomics viewer. Nat. Biotechnol. 29, 24–26 (2011)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d86e3143">66</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Repeat annotation.</h3><p>Known repeats were annotated using RepeatMasker with Rebase TE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Jurka, J. et al. Repbase Update, a database of eukaryotic repetitive elements. Cytogenet. Genome Res. 110, 462–467 (2005)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d86e3156">67</a></sup>, TIGR/MSU repeat<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Ouyang, S. et al. The TIGR Rice Genome Annotation Resource: improvements and new features. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, D883–D887 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d86e3160">57</a></sup> and in-house <i>Oryza</i> TE databases. <i>De novo</i> repeats were identified with RepeatScout<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Price, A.L., Jones, N.C. &amp; Pevzner, P.A. De novo identification of repeat families in large genomes. Bioinformatics 21 (suppl. 1), i351–i358 (2005)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d86e3170">68</a></sup>. RepeatMasker and LTR-FINDER<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Xu, Z. &amp; Wang, H. LTR_FINDER: an efficient tool for the prediction of full-length LTR retrotransposons. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, W265–W268 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d86e3175">69</a></sup> were used to identify complete LTR-RTs by examination of target site duplications (TSDs), primer binding sites, polypurinic tracts and element boundaries. Putative solo LTRs were identified by comparing the RepeatMasker match length with the LTR query length. Solo LTR candidates were then manually inspected for evidence of TSDs.</p><p>The 5′ and 3′ ends (40 bp per end) of an <i>O. sativa</i> complete Helitron data set were mapped to identify putative Helitrons in <i>O. glaberrima</i> using RepeatMasker with the following rules: (i) the 5′ and 3′ ends should be aligned within a distance of 1–20 kb on concordant strands with the expected orientation, (ii) allow less than four mismatches for the 5′ end and one mismatch in the 3′ CTAG end and (iii) inspect for insertion at the dinucleotide AT.</p><p>SINEs were identified using the strategy outlined in Baucom <i>et al</i>.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Baucom, R.S. et al. Exceptional diversity, non-random distribution, and rapid evolution of retroelements in the B73 maize genome. PLoS Genet. 5, e1000732 (2009)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d86e3194">70</a></sup>. MITE sequences were identified by searching for inverted repeats that were flanked by TSDs (2 bp for Stowaway and 3 bp for Tourist). For Stowaway, we searched specifically for the canonical terminal inverted repeat motif CTCCTCCC and a TA target site duplication. Terminal inverted repeats of at least 8 bp that started with a G or C were considered for Tourist elements. Approximately 400 candidate sequences were used for a multiple alignment with CLUSTALW<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Thompson, J.D., Higgins, D.G. &amp; Gibson, T.J. Clustal-W—improving the sensitivity of progressive multiple sequence alignment through sequence weighting, position-specific gap penalties and weight matrix choice. Nucleic Acids Res. 22, 4673–4680 (1994)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d86e3198">71</a></sup> to identify groups, and redundancy (for example, forward and reverse sequences of the same family) was removed to yield the initial set of families. Consensus sequences were mapped to the genome by BLASTN to identify all copies for each family.</p><p>Identified repetitive elements were further characterized and classified using the criteria described by Wicker <i>et al</i>.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Wicker, T. et al. A unified classification system for eukaryotic transposable elements. Nat. Rev. Genet. 8, 973–982 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d86e3208">72</a></sup>, with the exception of LTR-RTs. An LTR-RT was assigned to a family based on the best BLAST hit against RepBase. Insertion times of complete LTR-RT elements were estimated using a molecular paleontology approach described by SanMiguel <i>et al</i>.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="SanMiguel, P., Gaut, B.S., Tikhonov, A., Nakajima, Y. &amp; Bennetzen, J.L. The paleontology of intergene retrotransposons of maize. Nat. Genet. 20, 43–45 (1998)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d86e3215">73</a></sup>, with a mutation rate of 1.3 × 10<sup>−8</sup> substitutions per site per year, as proposed by Ma and Bennetzen<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Ma, J. &amp; Bennetzen, J.L. Rapid recent growth and divergence of rice nuclear genomes. Proc. Natl. Acad. Sci. USA 101, 12404–12410 (2004)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d86e3222">74</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">Sample preparation and sequencing for evolutionary analysis.</h3><p>The <i>O. glaberrima</i> and <i>O. barthii</i> accessions (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.3044#MOESM2">Supplementary Tables 12</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.3044#MOESM2">14</a>) were obtained from the African Rice Center (ARC) and IRRI-GRC. The <i>O. sativa</i> ssp. <i>japonica</i> accessions were obtained from IRRI-GRC. Leaf tissue was collected for each accession at the five-leaf stage, and genomic DNAs were extracted for sequencing using Qiagen DNeasy Plant Mini kits (Qiagen, Maryland, USA) following the manufacturer's protocol. GAIIx libraries were constructed using Illumina standard adaptors and sequenced on an Illumina GAIIx instrument with 2 × 75-bp sequencing chemistry. HiSeq libraries were constructed on a SPRIworks System I (Beckman Coulter, USA) with custom MID adaptors as described in Huang <i>et al</i>. (2009)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Huang, X. et al. High-throughput genotyping by whole-genome resequencing. Genome Res. 19, 1068–1076 (2009)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d86e3256">75</a></sup> and sequenced on an Illumina HiSeq 2000 instrument using 2 × 100-bp cycle sequencing chemistry. For <i>O. barthii</i> accessions sequenced with 5× coverage, 20 individuals were sequenced in one lane of the HiSeq 2000 instrument. For other accessions, one individual was sequenced in one lane of the GAIIx instrument, or five individuals were sequenced in one lane of the HiSeq 2000 instrument.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17">SNP detection.</h3><p>Sequence reads from <i>O. glaberrima</i> and <i>O. barthii</i> accessions were separated according to the 3-bp barcode added in the adaptor using custom Perl scripts. Burrows-Wheeler Aligner (BWA) V0.5.9 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Fast and accurate long-read alignment with Burrows-Wheeler transform. Bioinformatics 26, 589–595 (2010)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d86e3276">76</a>) was used to map raw pair-end reads onto the <i>O. glaberrima</i> CG14 genome assembly. All reads with a mapping quality score of less than 20 were discarded. The mean coverage of each accession was evaluated using BEDtools V2.13.3 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Quinlan, A.R. &amp; Hall, I.M. BEDTools: a flexible suite of utilities for comparing genomic features. Bioinformatics 26, 841–842 (2010)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d86e3282">77</a>). Alignment files were then input into Genome Analysis Toolkit (GATK) V1.2 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="McKenna, A. et al. The Genome Analysis Toolkit: a MapReduce framework for analyzing next-generation DNA sequencing data. Genome Res. 20, 1297–1303 (2010)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d86e3286">78</a>) to identify SNPs. Multiple SNP calling was performed using the UnifiedGenotyper from GATK. SNPs were filtered for quality score &gt;20, coverage greater than two and less than twice the mean coverage of all accessions. A SNP was retained if more than one accession had the SNP called at the identical position.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec18">History of <i>O. glaberrima</i> domestication.</h3><p>Several methods were applied to identify the population structure of <i>O. barthii</i>. First, the SNPs of the <i>O. barthii</i> population were loaded into the program ADMIXTURE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Alexander, D.H., Novembre, J. &amp; Lange, K. Fast model-based estimation of ancestry in unrelated individuals. Genome Res. 19, 1655–1664 (2009)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d86e3308">23</a></sup> to perform maximum likelihood clustering analysis. The result from ADMIXTURE was plotted using an R script. Second, a NJ tree of the <i>O. barthii</i> population was constructed for all SNP positions using the program Phylip with 1,000 bootstrap steps. Third, PCA was performed to assess the population structure of <i>O. barthii</i> using SMARTPCA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="Patterson, N., Price, A.L. &amp; Reich, D. Population structure and eigenanalysis. PLoS Genet. 2, e190 (2006)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d86e3319">79</a></sup>. The result of PCA was plotted using an R script. Finally, 10,000 SNP positions were randomly selected from the SNP set using a PERL script. The SNPs were input into the program PhyML 3.0 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Guindon, S. et al. New algorithms and methods to estimate maximum-likelihood phylogenies: assessing the performance of PhyML 3.0. Syst. Biol. 59, 307–321 (2010)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d86e3322">80</a>) to construct a maximum likelihood tree using the HKY85 model with 100 bootstrap steps.</p><p>In total, 8,374,445 SNPs were used to investigate the genetic relationship of <i>O. glaberrima</i> and <i>O. barthii</i>. Genetic differentiation (<i>F</i><sub>ST</sub>) between <i>O. glaberrima</i> and each of the <i>O. barthii</i> subpopulations was calculated using VCFtools V0.1.12 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="Danecek, P. et al. The variant call format and VCFtools. Bioinformatics 27, 2156–2158 (2011)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d86e3345">81</a>). The NJ tree of the <i>O. glaberrima</i> and <i>O. barthii</i> accessions was constructed for all SNP positions using the program Phylip with 1,000 bootstrap steps.</p><p>The country of origin for each <i>O. barthii</i> accession was obtained from ARC and IRRI-GRC. The proportions of <i>O. barthii</i> accessions from different subgroups were calculated for each country. The proportions of <i>O. barthii</i> accessions of different types were also calculated for each country.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19">Genetic variation analysis of <i>O. glaberrima</i> and <i>O. barthii</i>.</h3><p>Genome-wide genetic diversity (<i>π</i>) was calculated using VCFtools V0.1.12 and POPBAM V0.3 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Garrigan, D. POPBAM: tools for evolutionary analysis of short read sequence alignments. Evol. Bioinform. Online 9, 343–353 (2013)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d86e3384">43</a>) for nonoverlapping 100-kb windows across the genome. The genetic diversity (<i>π</i>) of all annotated genes and intergenic regions was calculated using POPBAM V0.3. The Wilcoxon test for comparing genome-wide <i>π</i> values of <i>O. glaberrima</i> and <i>O. barthii</i> was performed using an R script. The distribution and boxplot of <i>π</i> values were generated using an R script. In total, 3,373,099 SNPs were input into VCFtools V0.1.12 to identify the MAF for <i>O. glaberrima</i> and <i>O. barthii</i>. The MAF spectrum was plotted using an R script. The correlation coefficient (<i>r</i><sup>2</sup>) of alleles was calculated to measure LD level in <i>O. glaberrima</i> and <i>O. barthii</i> using plink V1.07 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Purcell, S. et al. PLINK: a tool set for whole-genome association and population-based linkage analyses. Am. J. Hum. Genet. 81, 559–575 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d86e3420">82</a>). The distance that the LD decays to half of the highest value was calculated, and then plotted, using an R script.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20">Identification of regions under artificial selection.</h3><p>The reduction of genetic diversity (<i>π</i><sub>w</sub>/<i>π</i><sub>c</sub>) was calculated for nonoverlapping 100-kb windows across the genome using VCFtools V0.1.12. The windows that were in the 2.5% right tail of the distribution (<i>π</i><sub>w</sub>/<i>π</i><sub>c</sub> &gt; 5.8) were selected as candidate regions. The distribution of <i>π</i><sub>w</sub>/<i>π</i><sub>c</sub> along the chromosome was plotted using an R script.</p><p>SweeD<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 83" title="Pavlidis, P., Zivkovic, D., Stamatakis, A. &amp; Alachiotis, N. SweeD: likelihood-based detection of selective sweeps in thousands of genomes. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 2224–2234 (2013)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d86e3460">83</a></sup> was used for detecting complete selective sweeps in the <i>O. glaberrima</i> genome with default settings. A total of 4,436,289 SNPs were input into the SweeD program after filtering some SNPs according to the program's requirements. This program implements the composite likelihood ratio statistic<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Nielsen, R. et al. Genomic scans for selective sweeps using SNP data. Genome Res. 15, 1566–1575 (2005)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d86e3467">30</a></sup>, which identifies regions with significant deviations from the neutral SFS and performs better with genome-wide SNP data than SweepFinder<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Nielsen, R. et al. Genomic scans for selective sweeps using SNP data. Genome Res. 15, 1566–1575 (2005)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d86e3471">30</a></sup> does. The <i>O. punctata</i> genome sequence (<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/?term=AVCL00000000.1">AVCL00000000.1</a>) was used to determine whether alleles were ancestral or derived in order to use the unfolded version of the SFS. Haplotypes were inferred using HapMap tools, and derived or ancestral alleles were identified using the genome sequence of <i>O. punctata</i>. A total of 1,746,642 SNPs were analyzed. We used the integrated haplotype score (iHS) statistic<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Voight, B.F., Kudaravalli, S., Wen, X. &amp; Pritchard, J.K. A map of recent positive selection in the human genome. PLoS Biol. 4, e72 (2006)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d86e3489">38</a></sup> to identify regions with unusually long haplotypes relative to the whole genome. Large negative values of iHS indicated high haplotype homozygosity because of an increase in frequency of the derived allele, and positive values reflected high frequency of the ancestral allele. Analyses were conducted using the R package rehh<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 84" title="Gautier, M. &amp; Vitalis, R. rehh: an R package to detect footprints of selection in genome-wide SNP data from haplotype structure. Bioinformatics 28, 1176–1177 (2012)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d86e3493">84</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">Evidence of independent domestication of <i>O. glaberrima</i>.</h3><p>To investigate the introgression of Asian rice into African rice, resequencing reads from 14 <i>O. sativa</i> and 20 <i>O. glaberrima</i> accessions (10–30× coverage) were mapped to the <i>O. glaberrima</i> RefSeq data using BWA V0.5.9. All reads with a mapping quality score of less than 20 were discarded. The alignment files of the <i>O. sativa</i> and <i>O. glaberrima</i> accessions were then input into POPBAM V0.3 to detect evidence of introgression from <i>O. sativa</i> into <i>O. glaberrima</i> using the recently developed <i>G</i><sub>min</sub> statistic<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Geneva, A.J., Lovato, L.M., Kingan, S.B. &amp; Garrigan, D. A new method to scan genomes for introgression in a secondary contact model. 
http://arxiv.org/abs/1403.1552

 (2014)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d86e3536">42</a></sup>.</p><p><i>O. sativa</i> domestication genes were selected according to criteria described in Meyer and Purugganan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Meyer, R.S. &amp; Purugganan, M.D. Evolution of crop species: genetics of domestication and diversification. Nat. Rev. Genet. 14, 840–852 (2013)." href="/articles/ng.3044#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d86e3545">48</a></sup>. Orthologous genes of the <i>O. sativa</i> domestication genes in <i>O. glaberrima</i> were identified by nucleotide and amino acid BLAST searches. The Tajima's <i>D</i> value of annotated genes and intergenic regions was calculated using POPBAM V0.3. The Tajima's <i>D</i> value of <i>O. glaberrima</i> orthologs of domestication genes was calculated using POPBAM V0.3. The reduction of diversity (<i>π</i><sub>w</sub>/<i>π</i><sub>c</sub>) of genes that deviated significantly from neutrality was calculated for 300-bp sliding windows with 200-bp overlapping using the SNPs generated from 20 <i>O. glaberrima</i> and 19 <i>O. barthii</i> accessions using VCFtools V0.1.12. Distributions of the reduction of diversity of genes were plotted using an R script.</p><p>To identify the <i>OsSh1</i> orthologous region, five upstream and downstream genes from <i>OsSh1</i> (LOC_Os03g44710) were mapped to the <i>O. glaberrima</i> genome. Two BAC clones encompassing the <i>OsSh1</i> region (OG_BBa0035M03 for <i>O. glaberrima</i> and OB_ABa0085D15 for <i>O. barthii</i>) were selected by aligning BAC-end sequences to the <i>O. sativa</i> ssp. <i>japonica</i> and <i>O. glaberrima</i> genomes. Two different insert libraries (500 bp and 10 kb) were constructed, sequenced and assembled using a Pacific Biosciences RS II instrument and HGAP software according to the manufacturer's recommendations. Both BACs were assembled into single contigs (139,241 bp for OG_BBa0035M03 and 176,785 bp for OB_ABa0085D15) without further finishing efforts. Sequence comparisons were performed using Dotter and Nucmer, and orthologs were identified using Nucmer and BLAST. To identify the <i>Sh4</i> orthologous region, <i>Sh4</i> gene sequences from <i>O. sativa</i> ssp. <i>japonica</i> were mapped to the <i>O. glaberrima</i> genome sequences. One BAC clone encompassing <i>Sh4</i> in <i>O. glaberrima</i> (OG_BBa0063K01) was selected. The BAC was assembled into a single contig (175,355 bp) without further finishing efforts using the same method described above. Sequence comparisons were performed using BLAST. The orthologous gene of <i>qSh1</i> was identified and compared using BLAST and manual inspection.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec22">URLs.</h3><p>RepeatMasker, <a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org/">http://www.repeatmasker.org/</a>; SNPs used for <i>O. barthii</i> population structure analysis and for investigating the genetic relationship of <i>O. glaberrima</i> and <i>O. barthii</i> can be downloaded at <a href="http://de.iplantcollaborative.org/dl/d/11EA9662-D292-4C64-8862-69466C087936/Oglaberrima_Obarthii_population_variation.vcf">http://de.iplantcollaborative.org/dl/d/11EA9662-D292-4C64-8862-69466C087936/Oglaberrima_Obarthii_population_variation.vcf</a>; SNPs used for the study of genetic variation of <i>O. glaberrima</i> and <i>O. barthii</i> can be downloaded at <a href="http://ensembl.gramene.org/Oryza_glaberrima/Info/Index">http://ensembl.gramene.org/Oryza_glaberrima/Info/Index</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec23">Accession codes.</h3><p>The assembly and annotation of the <i>O. glaberrima</i> genome are available at <a href="http://ensembl.gramene.org/Oryza_glaberrima/Info/Index">http://ensembl.gramene.org/Oryza_glaberrima/Info/Index</a> and have been deposited under GenBank accession number <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/?term=ADWL00000000.1">ADWL00000000.1</a>. The assembly of the <i>Oryza punctata</i> genome has been deposited under GenBank accession number <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/?term=AVCL00000000.1">AVCL00000000.1</a>. The BAC sequence assemblies have been deposited under GenBank accession numbers <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/?term=KF284071">KF284071</a>, <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/?term=KF284072">KF284072</a> and <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/?term=KJ650506">KJ650506</a>. The resequencing reads of <i>O. glaberrima</i>, <i>O. barthii</i>, <i>O. sativa</i> ssp. <i>japonica</i> and <i>O. sativa</i> ssp. <i>indica</i> have been deposited under GenBank accession numbers <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX502298">SRX502298</a>–<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX502317">SRX502317</a>, <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX502162">SRX502162</a>–<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX502255">SRX502255</a>, <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX621487">SRX621487</a>–<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX621493">SRX621493</a> and <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX621496">SRX621496</a>–<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX621502">SRX621502</a>, respectively. The RNA-Seq reads of <i>O. sativa</i> ssp. <i>japonica</i> leaf, panicle and root have been deposited under GenBank accession numbers <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX477950">SRX477950</a>, <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX477951">SRX477951</a> and <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX477952">SRX477952</a>, respectively. The RNA-Seq reads of <i>O. glaberrima</i> leaf, panicle and root have been deposited under GenBank accession numbers <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX474528">SRX474528</a>, <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX474529">SRX474529</a> and <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX474530">SRX474530</a>, respectively. The RNA-Seq reads of leaf and panicle of <i>O. barthii</i>, <i>O. rufipogon</i> and <i>O. nivara</i> have been deposited under GenBank accession numbers <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX471823">SRX471823</a>, <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX472434">SRX472434</a>, <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX512340">SRX512340</a>, <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX512341">SRX512341</a>, <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX472708">SRX472708</a> and <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRX472710">SRX472710</a> respectively.</p></div></div></section>

                        <span class="c-article-identifiers"><a class="c-article-identifiers__item" href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=search&amp;term=Rod A+Wing" data-track="click" data-track-action="author link - pubmed" data-track-label="link">PubMed</a><span class="u-hide"> </span><a class="c-article-identifiers__item" href="http://scholar.google.co.uk/scholar?as_q=&amp;num=10&amp;btnG=Search+Scholar&amp;as_epq=&amp;as_oq=&amp;as_eq=&amp;as_occt=any&amp;as_sauthors=%22Rod A+Wing%22&amp;as_publication=&amp;as_ylo=&amp;as_yhi=&amp;as_allsubj=all&amp;hl=en" data-track="click" data-track-action="author link - scholar" data-track-label="link">Google Scholar</a></span></p></div></div></li></ol></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="contributions">Contributions</h3><p>M. Wang performed all population sequencing and light response gene analyses. M. Wang and C.A.M. performed the population genomic analysis. Y.Y. directed all genome sequencing efforts. G.H. performed all genome-wide gene and tRNA annotations and the analysis of tandemly duplicated genes. P.R.M. assembled the <i>O. glaberrima</i> genome. C.F. performed all flowering time genes analyses. C.F. and M. Wang performed domestication-genes artificial selection analysis. J.L.G. edited the <i>O. glaberrima</i> physical map and selected the MTP. A.Z., R.M.C., O.P. and T.W. performed all repeat annotation and analyses. X.S., M. Wang, Y.Y. and D.K. performed analysis of the shattering genes. D.K. and J.S.S.A. performed overall project management. C.M. performed all WRKY gene family analyses. S.L., N.S., K.d.B., W.G., M. Wissotski and W.K. performed all hands-on activities related to <i>O. glaberrima</i> genome sequencing. P.S. grew, validated and maintained all <i>Oryza</i> accessions used in the project. M.-N.N. and K.S. provided all <i>O. barthii</i> accessions used for population genomics analysis. M.L. provided advice on the analysis of molecular evolution and population genomic data. J. Carney provided advice and consultation on the geographical and historical aspects of west African rice and slavery. M.C. and J. Chen provided early access to the <i>O. brachyantha</i> genome sequence and general consultation throughout the project. Y.Y., S.R., K.F.X.M., M.C. and R.A.W. conceived and guided the entire project and wrote the paper with contributions and input from all project members.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="corresponding-author">Corresponding authors</h3><p id="corresponding-author-list">Correspondence to
                <a id="corresp-c1" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/ng.3044/email/correspondent/c1/new">Mingsheng Chen</a> or <a id="corresp-c2" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/ng.3044/email/correspondent/c2/new">Klaus F X Mayer</a> or <a id="corresp-c3" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/ng.3044/email/correspondent/c3/new">Steve Rounsley</a> or <a id="corresp-c4" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/ng.3044/email/correspondent/c4/new">Rod A Wing</a>.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="ethics" data-title="Ethics declarations"><div class="c-article-section" id="ethics-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="ethics">Ethics declarations</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="ethics-content">
              
                <h3 class="c-article__sub-heading">Competing interests</h3>
